<div id="review_2675936211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2675936211" />
    <a title=" Teodora " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"><img alt=" Teodora " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582144281p2/69603149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2675936211?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=on-app">on-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2675936211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12482360372576093858">4.5/5 ⭐<br/><br/><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/02/08/the-cruel-prince-the-folk-of-the-air-1-by-holly-black/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br/><br/><i>
  <b>“(…) cheekbones sharp enough to cut out a girl’s heart.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>I love me a cruel and tipsy Faerie prince and that’s Cardan and only Cardan.<br/><br/>I mean everything I said in the previous sentence. Every. Word. Is. True.<br/><br/>Cardan was the best thing happening to this book and if you deny this that that’s strictly your problem. He’s a charmer.<br/><br/>*<br/><br/>I don’t read hyper-hyped books in general. But when I do, I read them aeons after they’re out so the hype has worn out</span>
  <span id="freeText12482360372576093858" style="display:none">4.5/5 ⭐<br><br><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/02/08/the-cruel-prince-the-folk-of-the-air-1-by-holly-black/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br><br><i>
  <b>“(…) cheekbones sharp enough to cut out a girl’s heart.”</b>
</i><br><br>I love me a cruel and tipsy Faerie prince and that’s Cardan and only Cardan.<br><br>I mean everything I said in the previous sentence. Every. Word. Is. True.<br><br>Cardan was the best thing happening to this book and if you deny this that that’s strictly your problem. He’s a charmer.<br><br>*<br><br>I don’t read hyper-hyped books in general. But when I do, I read them aeons after they’re out so the hype has worn out and I can enjoy the book (or not) in peace. This one was super hyped. I was plainly curious to see if it really is worth a shot.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1576246241ra/28605459.gif" width="302" height="302" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I truly didn’t expect the beginning of the book to <i>scream</i> like that. That was a power move. And I liked it.<br><br>Everything that came after that was to lure us into the Faerie world, of what, I must admit, I have only a minimum knowledge of. Everyone is beautiful, but everyone is cruel. Basically, it looks like a circus.<br><br>It is important for me to be able to grasp the world from the beginning. I feel frustrated when the whole universe unravels as if I just dropped in the middle of what was going on and no one had the time to acknowledge me. <i>I want to feel important from the beginning.</i><br>Thank you, Holly Black, I did feel important!<br><br><i>
  <b>“Being born mortal is like being born already dead.”</b>
</i><br><br>This is the story of sisters. Vivienne, Jude and Taryn are three sisters who began their lives in the mortal world and but then were forced to come to Elfhame after their parents got brutally murdered by their soon-to-be foster father – Vivienne’s real father. Vivi is one of them; Jude and Taryn, the twins, are not. This is the story of the sisters’ struggle to be accepted in a world that doesn’t want them to be part of. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576246241i/28605460.png" width="308" height="334" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Although Jude and Taryn are twins, they are completely different from each other. Where Taryn is ladylike and delicate, silent and obedient, Jude is determined and loud and wild. Where Taryn wants to be granted a place in the Faerie world through marriage, Jude wants to be a knight and play at war.<br><br>The story is narrated from Jude’s point of view. That is probably why many people find her annoying. The whole story sounds like her own roaring thoughts and feelings. Maybe she annoys herself too as many of us get annoyed with ourselves and our own thoughts.<br><br><i>
  <b>“You’re like a story that hasn’t happened yet.”</b>
</i><br><br>In a purely honest note, I kind of liked Jude in this book. Sure, she was a bit annoying sometimes, but truth be said, I liked her better than Taryn. There was something about her twin sister that made me repel her. Jude was interesting in a way that made me relate to her. I could totally see me sometimes in her actions. I felt like she was full of her own personality.<br><br>She’s power-thirsty. But this is how she was raised to be. To fight, to scheme, to seek and seize power. She’s the foster daughter of the great general of the Faerie after all. I still consider that a badass trait about her. Don’t you think?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441693597ra/16140063.gif" width="302" height="212" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, as I previously stated, I think I might have a soft spot for Cardan, the youngest Prince of the Faerie.<br><br><i>
  <b>“There’s safety in being awful.”</b>
</i><br><br>Cardan Greenbriar might seem cruel, reckless, thirsty for violence, but I think he is totally the good boy in disguise type. I mean, at first, I couldn’t stand him (even though I hated his friends more than I despised him). Then, there was this period of transition where I had mixed feelings about him. 65% in and I just slowly but steadily started to fall in love with him. I started to realise things about him as presented by his actual, intimate actions. And how couldn’t I fall like a fool? He was a lonely and broken boy. All he wanted was to love and be loved, but no one seemed to care about him enough to grant him that little. What is the whole power in the world of Faerie without an ounce of affection to it?<br><br><i>
  <b>“Most of all, I hate you because I think of you. Often. It’s disgusting and I can’t stop.”</b>
</i><br><br>He hates. Hates because he loves. Hate because he’s not loved.<br><br>His relationship with Jude starts and unfolds slowly. They have that wonderful love-to-hate relationship that I actually enjoy in books in general.<br><br>I consider their relationship a bit unhealthy though. What happens between the two of them is a peculiar kind of hate-love. It’s a game played out of spite. It’s all about power and desire. I am not sure this is right, but I do believe that this type of relationship is going to improve because from hate to love to hate to love again – that’s an endless wheel that could be stopped anytime, anywhere. One can make a beautiful thing out of something hideous, but one can also ruin the beauty of a thing. Their relationship, in this book, is dangerous ground.<br><br>Indeed, something about the book seemed off. Even though the world-building was very good and the action was fantastic, the depth of the characters was somehow missing. I wanted them to be more individualised, but I think that’s just because we see the story through only one character’s point of view. When you personalise the action, it’s hard to create well-developed individuals.<br><br>That, I think, it’s the only contradictory thing I have to say about this book. Really. I even enjoyed all the bloodshed there. And that’s not okay. But it was so cleverly crafted that I just <i>had to</i> enjoy it somehow??<br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>Also see:</b><br>#2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2675936102" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wicked King</a> (⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐)<br>#3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2763398749?type=review#rating_277176610" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Nothing</a> (⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐)<br><br><br>(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/55548670-d691-4ef0-a931-e51b9839cf30_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-inspired</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12482360372576093858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2018">z-faves2018</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-notowned">y-notowned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2018">y-out2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1961496305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1375836122384054294">...I have no idea how this review got deleted, but here is a reupload from my blog! <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>If I cannot be better than them, I will be so much worse.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>God, this book killed me. <i>The Cruel Prince</i> has just about what you’d expect from Black: court intrigue, an atmosphere of terror, vaguely dark romance, and a main character who is a terrible person, but is also so interesting. Plus some interesting dynamics and setup for an even better sequel. Needless to say, I found it delightful.<br/><br/>I think Black’</span>
  <span id="freeText1375836122384054294" style="display:none">...I have no idea how this review got deleted, but here is a reupload from my blog! <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>If I cannot be better than them, I will be so much worse.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />God, this book killed me. <i>The Cruel Prince</i> has just about what you’d expect from Black: court intrigue, an atmosphere of terror, vaguely dark romance, and a main character who is a terrible person, but is also so interesting. Plus some interesting dynamics and setup for an even better sequel. Needless to say, I found it delightful.<br /><br />I think Black’s tendency is to start a story with a badass opening, then spend 200 pages on slow buildup. At first I thought it was just because this is a series beginner, but the more I think about it, the more I realize her stories never have a typical growth and climax. Instead, she slowly escalates tension until suddenly the situation is horrible and you’re left wondering how these characters even got there. It’s an odd style, and one that will be divisive among readers, but it works for me.<br /><br />The plot here is just as slow-burning as usual, perhaps even more so. I personally thought it suited the story quite well. Even when I was slumping, this book was easy to come back to and enjoy. I have to admit, at spots the court intrigue got confusing. Main characters were easy to remember, but I couldn’t tell most of the Elder King’s children apart.<br /><br />Maybe my favorite part of this book was the character work. Holly Black is very talented at getting side characters to read real, even without much focus on them. But the real strength of this book is Jude’s flawed, morally grey character. I fucking loved her. She’s not the greatest person, but she’s so incredibly aware of it that I found it hard not to love her.<br /><br />I also wanted to spare a paragraph for the romance. There is a sort-of romance in the first half, and it is honestly the weakest part of the first three-quarters. (See my updates for this book.)<br /><br />Thankfully, this thrown-in and tensionless romance is improved upon further into the book. I’m not going to spoil it, exactly, but we all know Black loves her Hades/Persephone-esque dynamics. The dynamic between the two characters who I think will get together really turned me off in the first half; I was looking out for some kind of lacking-in-consent bad-boys-are-hawt type thing. That’s not what you’ll find here. This is much more of a genuine Hades/Persephone dynamic than a bad-boys-are-hot romance. I’ve written about the difference before on my blog, but this is one of the better handlings of it I’ve seen. There was one scene in this book between them that… well, I think my brain just screamed “holy shit” for a minute straight. One of those scenes I’m going to bookmark and reread over and over again.<br /><br />Anyway, I definitely loved this. When is book two coming out again?<br /><br />Brief note before I finish this review, and this doesn’t need much commentary: Ben and Severin had a cameo in this. I almost cried, embarrassingly enough. The Darkest Part of the Forest is one of my favorite books ever. According to a couple other reviews, some of the side characters are also cameos from her first fae series, if you’re at all interested! I didn’t notice because I’ve never read it. But I do like that she’s built a whole world, without requiring you to read every book for comprehension. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://sptfy.com/4F6I" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify</a> | <a href="https://thebookishactress.carrd.co/" rel="nofollow noopener">About</a> | </span>
  <a data-text-id="1375836122384054294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2048033820" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2048033820" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2048033820?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=fantasy-series">fantasy-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2048033820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13598962364915581801"><i>”Faeries make up for their inability to lie with a panoply of deceptions and cruelties. Twisted words, pranks, omissions, riddles, scandals, not to mention their revenges upon one another for ancient, half-remembered slights. Storms are less fickle than they are, seas less capricious.”</i><br/><br/>And this is exactly why I <u>
  <b>LOVED</b>
</u> this book! I dunno about you but I love my faeries wicked, cunning and cruel and unfortunately not a lot of authors are able to pull that off. Many faerie books are pretty soft a</span>
  <span id="freeText13598962364915581801" style="display:none"><i>”Faeries make up for their inability to lie with a panoply of deceptions and cruelties. Twisted words, pranks, omissions, riddles, scandals, not to mention their revenges upon one another for ancient, half-remembered slights. Storms are less fickle than they are, seas less capricious.”</i><br /><br />And this is exactly why I <u>
  <b>LOVED</b>
</u> this book! I dunno about you but I love my faeries wicked, cunning and cruel and unfortunately not a lot of authors are able to pull that off. Many faerie books are pretty soft and the MCs are like Twilight’s Bella and Edward only that they are faeries instead of vampires. So I’m always beyond excited and more than just a little delighted (oopsie that rhymed again, <s>I can’t hide my faerie heritage after all</s>) when I find a book and an author that actually knows about the true legends and fairy tales. <br /><br />What it comes down to is that Holly Black definitely is one of those mentioned authors! I swear, I didn’t have as much fun reading a faerie book ever since I finished Melika Dannese’s “Deadmarsh Fey” and Melissa Marr’s “Wicked Lovely” series. If you don’t know either of those two you better check them out and see if they might be something for you. ;-) I admit they aren’t for everyone because they stick to the facts of legends and myths (especially Melika’s book) but if you’re into well researched books and want something that’s close to the common folk tales but still has its own voice I can totally recommend them. <br /><br />Anyway! After finishing <b>“The Cruel Prince”</b> I was so satisfied, I felt like I needed the proverbial cigarette after. Since I don’t smoke I settled for a whiskey instead and enjoyed one of those rare silent evenings when you’re able to let your thoughts wander. In the end I can say that I loved all the characters and their duplicity and I’m definitely craving for more! I can’t wait to read “The Wicked King” soon, but for now you’ll just have to endure one of my long and super spoilery reviews. This is how faeries are done and I’m so going to write an essay about it! *lol* If you want to read my full review you can do it <a href="https://thesassylibraryfox.wordpress.com/2019/11/09/review-the-cruel-prince-holly-black/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>! <br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>You’re leaving the mortal realm and are now entering Faerie. Keep your friends close to you, don’t accept dance proposals and if any food is offered to you and you take it… well, then you’re already doomed. XD Spoilers ahead of you. Be my guest! And btw did I mention that it would be a pleasure to dance with you? *offers hand* ;-P</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Jude:</b><br /><br /><i>”No matter how careful I am, eventually I’ll make another misstep. I am weak. I am fragile. I am mortal. I hate that most of all. Even if, by some miracle, I could be better than them, I will never be one of them.”</i><br /><br />Ahhh now Jude is what I call a driven character! That girl’s on fire and no matter what kind of obstacle is in her way she’s ready to take it up with the entire world. I kinda like her for it. *lol* I mean she’s very self-conscious, she knows her limits and that she’ll never become one of the faeries she lives with but she’s still sort of brave and reckless. Just because she’s a human and weak in comparison to all the others this doesn’t mean that she’ll back down. Jude might be human but she won’t allow her weaknesses to define her and that’s amazing! I know many people might think that she’s dumb for even trying and that she should keep her head down just like her twin sister Taryn, but if you’re constantly being picked at there comes a point where you can’t and won’t take it any longer. I loved that Jude is courageous enough to take that extra step, to do what no one expects her to do and to laugh in their faces even if they are trying to push her down. Is it dangerous? You bet it is. Was it fun to watch Jude dish out retaliation to those obnoxious faeries? <b>HELL YES</b>!!! I adore my cunning and determined baby and I can’t wait to see what she’s going to do next. XD<br /><br /><i>”I am going to keep on defying you. I am going to shame you with my defiance. You remind me that I am a mere mortal and you are a prince of Faerie. Well, let me remind you that means you have much to lose and I have nothing.”</i><br /><br /><i>”What could I become if I stopped worrying about death, about pain, about anything? If I stopped trying to belong? Instead of being afraid, I could become something to fear.”</i><br /><br /><i>”If I cannot be better than them, I will become so much worse.”</i><br /><br /><b>Locke:</b><br /><br /><i>”There is pleasure in being with them,” he says. “Taking what we wish, indulging in every terrible thought. There’s safety in being awful.”</i> <br /><br />Now that’s a character that had me yelling at the pages, in a good way of course. ;-) Haha! I can’t believe that none of them realized how dangerous Locke truly is! I never bought into his “lonely boy” façade and if you ask me that one is going to be big, big trouble in book two. He might have taken a backseat in “The Cruel Prince” at the ending but that was only because he enjoyed “watching the story unfold”. XD Locke is a perfect example of a trickster and his story, well, it’s not over yet. Not by a long shot! And tell you what? I can’t wait to see what that wicked young faerie is going to do next. *lol* He might have fooled Jude once but I’m sure she’s on guard now and knowing her she won’t let him off the hook so easily. He’s most certainly prepared for her revenge though so Cardan and Jude better tread carefully around him. ;-) That boy’s got skill and he’ll use every little bit of it to get what he craves and wants. I guess he already proved that he has absolutely no qualms about playing unfair. XD<br /><br /><i>”I like for things to happen, for stories to unfold. And if I can’t find a good enough story, I make one.” He looks every inch the trickster in that moment.</i><br /><br /><b>Cardan:</b><br /><br /><i>”And Cardan is even more beautiful than the rest, with black hair as iridescent as a raven’s wing and cheekbones sharp enough to cut out a girl’s heart.”</i><br /><br />Okay, let me get it down on this page: I LOVED Cardan that little **** (insert swear word of your choice here)! *lol* GAH! I didn’t see such an arrogant and obnoxious character ever since I finished Melissa Marr’s series. Cardan is so cocksure of himself that it was a pleasure to watch him in action. Like seriously! That boy!!! All tough and mean on the outside but once you see beyond that he’s vulnerable af! &lt;3 What was really curious about him was that he has a tail! XD No one ever mentioned that in the reviews I read and I loved how it was implied that he hides it because it’s giving away his feelings. If there was one thing I didn’t like then it was that he wasn’t an all too big part of the story. I would have loved to see more of him and I really hope that Holly Black will do me that favour in “The Wicked King”. There are so many sides of his character I didn’t see yet and I want to explore them layer by layer! (Double meaning totally intended here! *lol*)<br /><br /><i>”Do you know what mortal means? It means born to die. It means deserving of death. That’s what you are, what defines you – dying. And yet here you stand, determined to oppose me even as you rot away from the inside out, you corrupt, corrosive mortal creature. Tell me how that is. Do you really think you can win against me? Against a prince of Faerie?”</i><br /><br /><i>”You are terrifying. Nearly my whole family is dead, and while they never had much love for me, I don’t want to join them. I’ve spent all night worrying what you’re going to do, and I know exactly what I deserve. I have a reason to be nervous.”</i><br /><br /><b>Vivi:</b><br /><br /><i>”I think it broke Vivi’s heart to return, but she did it. And she stayed. Whatever else I can say about Vivi, when it really mattered, she stuck by us.”</i><br /><br />Why did no one ever mention that Jude and Taryn have a big sister?! I was like: WHAT?! when I started to read the book and the fact that she has a mortal girlfriend was even more intriguing! I mean yes, Vivi is a side-character but she’s a pretty cool one and seems to have her heart in the right place. I like her way more than I like Taryn and I wish Holly Black would have taken more time to flesh her out. So far all we know is that she’s a rebel, kind and wants to live in the mortal world, which isn’t an awful lot if you ask me. I really hope that’s going to change in book two though! =) <br /><br /><i>Vivienne shrugs, and I am reminded of how, despite her being my sister, we differ in ways that are hard to comprehend. “You did a brave thing. Be glad of that. Not everyone can be brave. I’m not always.”</i><br /><br /><b>The relationships and ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Jude &amp; Locke:</u><br /><br /><i>”I brace myself for more scorn, but then one corner of his mouth lifts. He winks, as if in acknowledgement of being caught out. As if we’re sharing a secret. As if he thinks I am not loathly, as though he does not find my mortality contagious.”</i><br /><br />ALL of my faerie instincts screamed “HELL NO!!!” when Locke started to show interest in Jude and as it seems I was right. I’ve to admit that I have a lot of respect for Locke though. I mean that boy managed to seduce and confuse Jude big time and this even though she’s so distrustful and basically only sees the bad in every faerie. That’s quite an achievement and one of the main reasons I love Locke. He’s a manipulative, conniving and intelligent bastard and their relationship was nothing but cold-blooded calculation. Ahh how I admire that kind of ambition. *lol* Anyway, we all know that Jude will do everything possible to settle that score so Ha! You better wrap up warmly, Locke and Taryn. There’s an ice storm coming right your way. ;-P <br /><br /><i>”It takes us a long time to wend our way back down the stairs. My hands are in his hair. His mouth is on my neck. My back is against the ancient stone wall. Everything is slow and perfect and makes no sense at all. This can’t be my life. This feels nothing like my life.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Do you love me enough to give me up?” I am sure my expression is stricken. He leans closer. “Isn’t that a test of love?”</i><br /><br /><u>Jude &amp; Taryn:</u><br /><br /><i>”You think I’m weak.”<br />“You are weak,” I tell her. “You’re weak and pathetic and I –“<br />“I’m a mirror,” she shouts. “I’m the mirror you don’t want to look at.”</i><br /><br />Well, if Taryn isn’t a two-faced snake then I dunno. There’s Jude trying to save her naïve and stupid sister, just to find out that our young and innocent girl is anything but! I knew there was something up with her and Locke and I was not surprised to find out the truth. Unfortunately this can’t be said about Jude and I’m pretty sure Taryn just gambled her only chance to win the award for “best twin sister”. Not that she ever stood a chance to get it. I mean she always let Jude struggle on her own, she never helped her, never tried to defend her, she just let those faeries do what they wanted and if Taryn would have been my sister I would have broken with her a long time ago. Guess Jude got to that point now as well. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><u>Jude &amp; Cardan:</u><br /><br /><i>”I hate him more than all the others. I hate him so much that sometimes when I look at him, I can hardly breathe.”</i> <br /><br />I ship them. HARD!!! I loved those two! This kind of hate-love is so damn intriguing I can’t even! It’s so rare to see it on page and boy did Holly Black surpass herself! There are those two people that hate each other so much that they want to kill each other yet at the same time they have this incredible attraction and can’t seem to be able to fight it. I’ll only say it once but: YAS!!!! This is the supreme discipline of a love-hate relationship and if it continues to be that good in book two I’ll be in seventh heaven and will savour every second! It’s obvious they want each other but whilst it was pretty evident that Jude hated Cardan more than he hated her, the same can’t be said for the ending of the book. I think at the end they might have switched roles and I’m more than just certain that Cardan hates Jude with a fierce passion now. She forced him to take over the throne, the one thing he never wanted and he’s bound to her. Ohh damn! This is going to be fun once the one year and one day is over! *lol* But until then we can expect deadly C.H.E.M.I.S.T.R.Y and I’m so ready for it! &lt;333<br /><br /><i>He leans in and closes his eyes. “Most of all, I hate you because I think of you. Often. It’s disgusting, and I can’t stop.”<br />I’m shocked into silence.<br />“Maybe you should shoot me after all,” he says, covering his face with one long-fingered hand.</i><br /><br /><i>I fix him with a look. “I can be charming. I charmed you, didn’t I?”<br />He rolls his eyes. “Do not expect others to share my depraved tastes.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Cardan looks at me with helpless rage. Then, the full minute of my command up, he rises slowly to his feet. The fury in his eyes is familiar, the glitter of them like banked fire, like coals burning hotter than flames ever could. This time I deserve it. I promised he was going to be able to walk away from the Court and all its manipulations. I promised he would be free from all this. I lied.”</i><br /><br /><u>Cardan &amp; Locke:</u><br /><br /><i>”Enough,” Locke says sharply to Cardan. He’s got his hands on my shoulders and is pulling me roughly to my feet. “I’m taking her home.”<br />“Are you, now?” Cardan asks him, eyebrows raised. “Interesting timing. You like the savor of a little humiliation, just not too much?”<br />“I hate it when you get like this.” Locke says under his breath.</i><br /><br />Okay, seriously. What is it with those two? *lol* There is something between them and I just can’t put my finger on it! Judging by Cardan’s comment Locke didn’t try anything with him yet, but I think Cardan might have a soft spot for Locke? I mean he basically admitted that he’s insulted because Locke never showed any interest in him. XD Is this one-sided? Or is there more to it? Mhmm… those two are a tough nut to crack but I’ll find out sooner or later! Hopefully “The Wicked King” will be revealing. If there is actually something I’ve to admit that I’d definitely ship it! *lol* <br /><br /><i>That makes his smile grow. “Maybe he didn’t. Maybe either of you would have done as his first mortal conquest. I believe his goal is to have both of you in the end.”<br />I don’t like any of this. “What about you?”<br />He gives me a quick, odd look. “Locke hasn’t gotten around to seducing me yet, if that’s what you’re asking. I suppose I should be insulted.”</i><br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />I loved everything about this book! From the scheming to the intrigue, from the duplicity to the bitter truth, from lovers to haters and the other way around… Written down on 370 pages of perfection there was basically everything I crave for in a good faerie book and I really couldn’t be even more delighted than I already am. &lt;3 This book was <b>AMAZING</b> and totally worth the hype! Enough said! ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13598962364915581801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2555997072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2555997072" />
    <a title="Mary S. R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r"><img alt="Mary S. R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597037601p2/75831724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2555997072?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary S. R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary S. R." href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r">Mary S. R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/51507084-the-cruel-prince">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">seekers of dark fairytales</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=faves">faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=dark">dark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2555997072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11457232367345421676">Once upon a time, a wicked girl with a cold, cold heart traipsed through a forest so light and stark. Trees of clean bark. Branches dangling with folk art. <b>And it was thus she came upon a hole so, so dark.</b><br/><br/>Our restless little devil looked through the hole and glimpsed trees of bark covered in blood, branches twisted and falling with a thud, screams coming out of the mud that had seen much brutal flood.<br/><br/>So the girl backed up, and ran, and jumped.<br/><br/><b>I fell into the <i>Holly Black</i> hole for fun so dark.<br/>And </b></span>
  <span id="freeText11457232367345421676" style="display:none">Once upon a time, a wicked girl with a cold, cold heart traipsed through a forest so light and stark. Trees of clean bark. Branches dangling with folk art. <b>And it was thus she came upon a hole so, so dark.</b><br><br>Our restless little devil looked through the hole and glimpsed trees of bark covered in blood, branches twisted and falling with a thud, screams coming out of the mud that had seen much brutal flood.<br><br>So the girl backed up, and ran, and jumped.<br><br><b>I fell into the <i>Holly Black</i> hole for fun so dark.<br>And now, it seems, I am stuck.<br>Oops.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Nice things don’t happen in storybooks,” Taryn says. “Or when they do happen, something bad happens next. Because otherwise the story would be boring, and no one would read it.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Before picking up <i>The Cruel Prince</i> I, of course, had expectations. No, scratch that, I didn’t have expectations, I never do, never dare hope—I usually try to not expect much of a book so I wouldn't be disappointed—what I had was simply assumptions about how it was gonna be. And I was completely and utterly wrong. <b>People make this seem like a romance-oriented book; it is not.</b> This book is less about the romance (<i>which only starts to show itself a little by the end</i>) and more about games, intrigue and, most importantly, the characters. It’s about anger. Betrayal. Revenge. Secrets and, above all, power. This is the dangerous tale of a human girl who grew up in faerieland and has endured much cruelty and pain, is bullied at school, because of being mortal and weak.<br><br>She will show you she is not.<br>Let no one call Jude Duarte <i>weak</i>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>That’s what comes of hungering for something: You forget to check if it’s rotten before you gobble it down.</i>
</blockquote><br>She will be the human who looks at all that faeries have, acknowledges that she, as a human, is unworthy of those things, still wants them anyways, and thus takes them. Faeries might always be better than her, but she can be much, much worse. It should not surprise you that I adore her, then.<br><br><b><i>The Cruel Prince</i> is a cruel, enchanting tale of a cruel, enchanting people in a cruel, enchanting world. And all that I said are the reasons why I will love it forever. With you, to the ends of time.</b> As always, you can check out my chosen soundtrack for the series at the end of the review—I went slightly wild there and made a mash up of the three books’ covers to create one for my playlist.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>The odd thing about ambition is this: You can acquire it like a fever, but it is not so easy to shed.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>CW</u>
</b> ➾ abuse, bullying, drugging, speciesism (faeries over humans rather than humans over animals), self harm<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600609285i/30131414._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>
  <b>✧ Storyline ✧</b>
</u><br><br>One ordinary night a not so ordinary man drops from the sky into an ordinary human neighborhood riding a not so ordinary horse. He dismounts and walks up to one of the many ordinary houses and, raising his not so ordinary fist, he knocks.<br><br>The night is no longer ordinary.<br><br>For inside the house, three little girls watch TV and eat fish sticks with ketchup. For one bears half-faerie blood, while the pair of full human twins do not. For an scared woman comes running from the kitchen and the man calls her wife and traitor. For he kills her and takes the three little girls to faerieland. For in Faerie, there are no fish sticks, no ketchup, and no television.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Because you’re like a story that hasn’t happened yet. Because I want to see what you will do. I want to be part of the unfolding of the tale.”</i>
</blockquote><br>What there is in Fearie is a court ruled by the High King, presiding over the three factions of the Seelie Court, the Unseelie court, and the wild fey. And that king has a general—a faerie whose wife left him pregnant with his heir, a faerie who slaughtered a family one not so ordinary night and took three human girls.<br><br>Jude is the youngest of the three, the younger twin, and she wants nothing more than to belong, craves nothing more than being knighted and a permanent part of the court. Even if most of the faeries hate humans; even if she is bullied at school by the youngest prince and his gang; even if she is belittled and bloodied and nearly killed. <b>So it should come as a surprise to no one that she would lie and spy and become a vengeful murderess who changes the game. It does anyways.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I am tired of caring,” I say. “Why should I?”<br>“Because they could kill you!”<br>“They better,” I say to her. “Because anything less than that isn’t going to work.”</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600609285i/30131414._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>
  <b>✧ Storytelling ✧</b>
</u><br><br>Shame on you, Mary, for waiting so long to pick up a masterpiece of <i>Holly Black</i>’s. <b>A tale so well told. A twisted fairytale so mesmerising. An atmosphere so immersive and pulsing. An eye for detail and consideration and clever themes and additions. A hand wielding words and metaphors as a master swordsman would a sword.</b><br><br>I read my first Black book and did not look back.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I’ve seen many impossible things. I have seen the acorn before the oak. I have seen the spark before the flame. But never have I seen such as this: A dead woman living. A child born from nothing.”</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600609285i/30131414._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>
  <b>✧ Characters ✧</b>
</u><br><br>★ <b>
  <i>Jude:</i>
</b> Call her a wrecking ball if you want, call her an annoying bitch if you dare, I would only say you don’t comprehend the joy of jumping into the canyon of anger, the peace in throwing rules and caution into the wind, the freedom in crossing the line and embracing the glorious beauty of revenge. “<i>It’s the thrill of leaping without being able to see the ground below you, right before you realize that’s called falling.</i>” I would say that you’ve never known the colours. I would say you are blind.<br><br>She is a prideful, unyielding fighter who hates being vulnerable, being controlled. She is a vengeful, violent liar who adores power, adores attention. <b>She is angry and dark and probably needs to see a therapist but, if you told her so, would most likely tell you to go eff yo self and that she can manage herself quite nicely thank you very much.</b> And if you think she’s starting to sound like me...then whatever do you mean *<i>smiles sweetly</i>*<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“If you hurt me, I wouldn’t cry. I would hurt you back.”</i>
</blockquote><br>I’d heard <b>criticism of Jude’s reaction to the trauma of her childhood</b> and agreed with it for the beginning chapters, but then I realised that it’s merely that she handles the trauma differently.<br><br>What Jude does is escape thinking about what happened, flee her feelings and fear; and it naturally results in her becoming out of touch with her emotions. She endures and pushes it into the back of her brain due to not knowing another way to cope and that’s the way that comes naturally to her. She is always afraid, always on alert, so she’s grown numb and used to it, so she’s turned tired and angry, so she lashes out. <b>In fact, her mental state is captured accurately, because our personality shapes our response to trauma the same way trauma shapes our personality.</b> She doesn’t have nightmares not because her trauma has been ignored, but because she can’t calm her nerves enough to even sleep.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Before, I never knew how far I would go. Now I believe I have the answer. I will go as far as there is to go. I will go way too far.</i>
</blockquote><br>And if you put that kind of personality under pressure, it acts much like an elastic object: springing upon release, going wild and hitting everything at close range. She was raised in a house of butchery by a man who delights in war and death and conflict. And because such a man was her father and such a man killed her father, this is the birth of a murderer. Her composed smiles coming unraveled, coming undone.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I thought I was supposed to be good and follow the rules. But I am done with being weak. I am done with being good. I think I am going to be something else.”</i>
</blockquote><br>★ <b>
  <i>Cardan:</i>
</b> A few months ago a friend of mine forced me to watch the kdrama <i>Boys Over Flowers</i> in exchange for me asking her to watch the BBC <i>Sherlock</i>; the deal was that we’d each watch 6 episodes of our respective shows and stop after that if we’re no longer interested. I, ofc, stopped after 6 because I just can’t connect with kdaramas. But I’m glad I watched those episodes, because I can now write this: <b>Cardan Greenbriar is literally and thoroughly Gu Jun-pyo from <i>Boys Over Flowers</i>.</b><br><br>But where I only found Jun-pyo entertaining, I <i>love</i> Cardan, probably because of Jude’s difference from the female lead of the show. With Jun-pyo it was just a petulant boyo lashing out and being angry and bullying and abusing a powerless girl (<i>who still got back at him impressively but still, their personalities where the opposites</i>) while with Cardan <i>it’s a sparring match</i>.<br><br>I called him “a simple old-school bully” the very first time we were introduced, and I was both right and wrong. Right because he is an old-school bully, yet wrong because he is not simply so but playfully; Cardan is a clever cruel prince, an angry spoiled/abused child, and a charming adorable coward. Too young, too weak, too mean, too precious! But not ambitious, not like Jude. <b>I blame you guys for being disappointed at first</b>; it was unfair to feel annoyed that he couldn’t fill the shoes I’d thought Holly Black was intending for him when she <i>wasn’t</i> intending those shoes for him. He has his own shiny shoes to stand in and THANK GOD.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“There’s safety in being awful.”</i>
</blockquote><br>✯ <b>
  <i>Locke:</i>
</b> First character who intrigued me with his bored, manipulative ways. I spent a long time just repeating <i>what’s his game what’s his game</i> in my notes, I swear, and I find it rather perfect that his game is just that—a game. This drama-loving fox is one I simultaneously want to kiss and kill and absolutely cannot get enough of.<br><br>✯ <b>
  <i>Taryn:</i>
</b> Jude’s twin sister is much like her while still being the opposite. She, too, wants to belong and would do anything to achieve it; she, too, can be cold and manipulative as the faeries and craves their exotic danger, growing used to recognising bad things as good; and she, too, has had to become something else to survive, something not so human. But where Jude is wildfire, she is ice; one is raging, the other composed. Both burn you in the end.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Desire is an odd thing. As soon as it’s sated, it transmutes. If we receive golden thread, we desire the golden needle.”</i>
</blockquote><br>☆ Those aren’t the only ones that made an impact: <i>
  <b>Madoc</b>
</i> with his anger issues and twisted love, <i>
  <b>Vivi</b>
</i> with her raging selfish heart that encourages the same trait in others, <i>
  <b>Oriana</b>
</i> who is way more than she seems. All layered, none all-evil, being a mix of cruel and gentle. I heard someone say this book has an all-Slytherin cast, and I’m inclined to agree—no wonder I enjoy them all so much.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600609285i/30131414._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>
  <b>✧ Relationships ✧</b>
</u><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Like taking a dare to run over knives, like an adrenaline strike of lightning, like the moment when you’ve swum too far out in the sea and there is no going back, only cold black water closing over your head.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>❥ <i>Romance:</i></b> Can I just say Chapter 25 &amp; 26? BECAUSE CHAPTER 25 &amp; 26! To be frank with you, I wasn’t sure at first about these two as I had my doubts regarding Cardan being someone who could possibly match Jude in strength, but I now adore them because I realised the nature of dynamic is a game where <i>she</i> is the one with the power (<i>while being terrified of him ever having any power</i>) and he is drawn to that. He likes to challenge her, question her, <i>try</i> to best her, while actually delighting in her holding a dagger at his throat.<br><br>They spar; they fight; they have (<i>more or less</i>) the same personality, liars and deceivers and and power-oriented people. <b>Their only difference is that he’s a pleasure-seeking coward where she’s a purposeful warrior, and that somehow makes them an even better match.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“He’s flint, you’re tinder.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>❥ <i>Familial Bonds:</i></b> I’ve already talked too much so I’ll just say that the sisterhood, brother-sister bond, father-daughter relationship...all are written tangibly, conveying the complicated and contradictory feelings that come with being a family (<i>and one so messed up as this</i>) quite perfectly. It was a gem to read.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600609285i/30131414._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>
  <b>✧ Worldbuilding ✧</b>
</u><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596210936i/29893560._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Faerie might be beautiful, but its beauty is like a golden stag’s carcass, crawling with maggots beneath his hide, ready to burst.</i>
</blockquote><br>This land of beautiful nightmares, these creatures of twilight and glamours, these clawed hands bearing nevermore and faerie fruit with their superstitious-like practices (<i>e.g. having a necklace of dried rowan berries or wearing your stockings inside out</i>) that are not simply superstitions, all serve to exceptionally bring this world into life and prove that world building is, indeed, Holly Black’s ultimate strength.<br><br><b>In the end, reading <i>The Cruel Prince</i> with its mythical magic and all the cruelties, deceptions, and (<i>hypocritical</i>) prejudice of its people, feels like wandering through a fairytale that chose the path on its left somewhere down the road, refusing to go right. And you bet I always choose the path on my left as well.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600609285i/30131414._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>
  <b>✧ Companions ✧</b>
</u><br><br><b>
  <i>Book series playlist:</i>

I am actually shocked by how much I enjoyed this. If I'm being honest, I didn't think I would. <br/><br/>I had previously read, <i>The Darkest Part of the Forest</i> by Black, and it was just okay for me.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560864434ra/27688014.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Going into this one, I was expecting angsty romance, whiny little girls and unlikable love interests.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464724067ra/19269287.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I am so happy to repor</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2239163596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11270670567381485240"><b>Well, despite marking this as "currently reading" (I put books there that I plan to read within the next week or two) I finally cracked this bad boy open today...and finished it in one three-hour siting.</b><br/><br/>So, if that's not an indication of something being a seriously above average read, I don't know what is. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516653288i/24899523._SY540_.jpg' width='282' height='376' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Jude was a really edgy, imperfect, relatable character and I really liked her. <br/><br/>So often, I want characters to do something - maybe say something or do something <i>I</i> want them to do in a specific</span>
  <span id="freeText11270670567381485240" style="display:none"><b>Well, despite marking this as "currently reading" (I put books there that I plan to read within the next week or two) I finally cracked this bad boy open today...and finished it in one three-hour siting.</b><br><br>So, if that's not an indication of something being a seriously above average read, I don't know what is. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516653288i/24899523._SY540_.jpg" width="282" height="376" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jude was a really edgy, imperfect, relatable character and I really liked her. <br><br>So often, I want characters to do something - maybe say something or do something <i>I</i> want them to do in a specific moment - and I am left feeling frustrated and annoyed when they don't. <br><br>They DON'T deliver the nasty comeback I feel someone so amazingly deserves. <br>They DON'T punch the face of the asshole who has done them wrong.<br>They DON'T say "fuck you" to the person who just betrayed them. <br><br>But, Jude?<br><br>Home girl DID all of those things and more and I loved it. <br><br>She saw that proverbial high road on some occasions, the one other characters sometimes begged her to take and she said:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517273664ra/24963283.gif" width="299" height="152" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Get it, girl. <br><br>On top of that, the plot here was pretty well thought out and I enjoyed the twists and turns, none of which felt convenient or trite. <br><br>It will definitely be interesting to see what happens with the plot and certain character relationships in the next book. <br><br>The wait will be long. <br><br>Oh and PS...fuck you, Taryn.<br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/SteamyReadsBlog/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490118337i/22283577.png" width="40" height="40" alt="Follow us on facebook" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.instagram.com/steamyreads/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490118337i/22283578.png" width="40" height="40" alt="Follow us on instagram" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://steamyreads.net/youtube/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490120705i/22283756.png" width="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://www.steamyreads.net" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490118159i/22283551._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<span id="freeTextContainer16958044571259231922">some books are born great, some achieve greatness, and some have greatness thrust upon them. <br/><br/>this book is all of the above. my mind simply cannot comprehend what i just read because its greatness transcends human understanding. what a blessed world we live in where this kind of greatness exists for us mere mortals. <br/><br/>i cant even fathom what sort of perfection <i>‘the wicked king’</i> will be. the last half of this book is one of the best build-ups to a sequel i have ever read. like, are you kidding me!? </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=book-bfs">book-bfs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1994545077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14789989983872344323">me reading the folk of the air trilogy in a day *spoilers*: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FLg5DOadIbY'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FLg5D...</a><br/><br/><br/><b>hi i'm chandler and this is my favorite book of all time</b><br/><br/>no for real, this book has EVERYTHING. but first off i just want to say that y'all have been SLEEPING on holly black. she is incredible and i genuinely love every single one of her books that i have read. so i guess it's not surprising that i loved this one. what did i love you may ask?<br/><br/>- the writing... HELLO! YES! how can a book that is short</span>
  <span id="freeText14789989983872344323" style="display:none">me reading the folk of the air trilogy in a day *spoilers*: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FLg5DOadIbY">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FLg5D...</a><br /><br /><br /><b>hi i'm chandler and this is my favorite book of all time</b><br /><br />no for real, this book has EVERYTHING. but first off i just want to say that y'all have been SLEEPING on holly black. she is incredible and i genuinely love every single one of her books that i have read. so i guess it's not surprising that i loved this one. what did i love you may ask?<br /><br />- the writing... HELLO! YES! how can a book that is short and straight forward in writing pack such a big punch. this is no SJM, overly complicated and long bullshit. holly black writes with intention.<br /><br />- the family... the theme of family in this was amazing. jude's relationship with madoc and her sisters was so realistic and nuanced that i felt like it could have existed in real life. i loved it.<br /><br />- the world... somehow it slipped past me in the description of this book but this is set in present day. there are malls and mcdonalds in the human world. how fucking cool is that??? super cool juxtaposition with the seemingly antiquated fae world.<br /><br />- jude... sweetie. you are awesome. you are a bad ass. your feelings are so fcking valid. also the way her feelings about cardan are described in this book... perfection. i seriously related to her which is rare. why are females in books so damn annoying usually? idk but jude IS NOT.<br /><br />- CARDAN... i mean do i really have to explain this one? he's perfect. (but i will say, dunno what y'all are talking about with him secretly being a soft boy... he is NOT. he's a dick, and i love him)<br /><br /><b> if you love yourself, go read this book.</b></span>

<div id="review_1770033673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1770033673" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1770033673?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=best-of-2018">best-of-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=faeries-elves">faeries-elves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1770033673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer102316021022492212"><b>“Nice things don’t happen in storybooks. Or when they do happen, something bad happens next. Because otherwise the story would be boring, and no one would read it.”</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547360255ra/26909347.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>PERFECT</b>. This book is <b>PERFECT</b>. So…<i>BUCKLE UP! ‘CAUSE YOU’RE IN FOR A WILD RIDE!</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547360255ra/26909348.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Holly Black, you are going to be the <i>DEATH</i> of me! I loved the <b>Spiderwick Chronicles</b> as a child (so cute!), mildly enjoyed the <b>Modern Faerie Tale</b> series (kinda cringey, not gonna lie :-/), appreciated <b>The Darkest Part of the Forest</b> (so much faery tale-esque w</span>
  <span id="freeText102316021022492212" style="display:none"><b>“Nice things don’t happen in storybooks. Or when they do happen, something bad happens next. Because otherwise the story would be boring, and no one would read it.”</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547360255ra/26909347.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>PERFECT</b>. This book is <b>PERFECT</b>. So…<i>BUCKLE UP! ‘CAUSE YOU’RE IN FOR A WILD RIDE!</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547360255ra/26909348.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Holly Black, you are going to be the <i>DEATH</i> of me! I loved the <b>Spiderwick Chronicles</b> as a child (so cute!), mildly enjoyed the <b>Modern Faerie Tale</b> series (kinda cringey, not gonna lie :-/), appreciated <b>The Darkest Part of the Forest</b> (so much faery tale-esque whimsy!), tolerated the <b>Coldest Girl in Coldtown</b> (vampires are passé, okay?), and adored the <b>Curse Workers</b> trilogy (a magical mafia, need I say any more?!)…but the <b>Folk in the Air</b> trilogy is on a <i>WHOLE ‘NOTHER LEVEL</i>!!! Authors’ writing obviously improve over time. That’s a given. But Holly Black practically did a 180° from her début, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/283495.Tithe_A_Modern_Faerie_Tale" title="Tithe A Modern Faerie Tale by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Tithe: A Modern Faerie Tale</a>, to this release, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032825.The_Cruel_Prince__The_Folk_of_the_Air___1_" title="The Cruel Prince (The Folk of the Air, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cruel Prince</a>. Both involve faeries, which Holly is known for as the <i>Queen of the Faeries</i> in YA literature (Yes, she predates Sarah J Maas, having practically kick-started the faerie obsession in YA in 2002), but the similarities end there. My goodness, <b>THIS BOOK</b>! The plot, the characters, the world, the romance, the political intrigue, the faery lore…anything you could possibly want from a novel is <i>HERE</i>! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547360255ra/26909349.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>WELCOME TO FAERIE.</b><br><br><i>“What they don’t realize is this: Yes, they frighten me, but I have always been scared, since the day I got here. I was raised by the man who murdered my parents, reared in a land of monsters. I live with that fear, let it settle into my bones, and ignore it. If I didn’t pretend not to be scared, I would hide under my owl-down coverlets in Madoc’s estate forever. I would lie there and scream until there was nothing left of me. I refuse to do that. I will not do that.”</i><br><br>Personally, part of my enjoyment of this book has to do with the <b>unpredictability</b> of the storyline itself, so I’ll be brief in terms of the plot. The prologue begins with your modern American <i>mortal</i> family: a mum, a dad, an older sister, and a younger set of twins. Lo and behold, a redcap faery, <b>General Madoc</b>, shows up, slaughters the parents, and takes the children back with him to Faerie. The older sister also happens to be Madoc’s biological daughter, making her half-faery. Fast forward a few years and the children have been reared as Gentry faery children, without truly belonging there. The older sister, <b>Vivienne</b>, longs to <i>return to the mortal realm</i> and disavow everything that makes her a faery. The twins on the other hand, <b>Jude and Taryn</b>, seek to find their places among their faery peers. They <i>want to belong</i>, despite not being faeries themselves. In fact, they are constantly bullied by <b>Prince Cardan</b> and his friends, <b>Locke, Nicasia, and Valerian</b>, but that doesn't deter them. Taryn wants to belong by <i>marriage</i> and Jude wants to belong by <i>knighthood</i>. The real question remains…just how far are they willing to go, in order to finally gain their <i>rightful place</i> in Faerie?<br><br><i>“If I cannot be better than them, I will become so much worse.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547360255ra/26909350.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Jude Duarte</b> has sky-rocketed to my <i>top 10 list of favourite protagonists</i>. She’s definitely no <i>Mary Sue</i> with her swordsmanship skills and political strategising! At Holly Black’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2254319811" rel="nofollow noopener">book signing</a> for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032887.The_Wicked_King__The_Folk_of_the_Air___2_" title="The Wicked King (The Folk of the Air, #2) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wicked King</a>, she stated that she intended for Jude to be the female version of the <i>antihero with a tragic backstory</i> trope, you know, with her parents being murdered before her eyes and being bullied throughout those <i>crucial</i> childhood development years. As a result, Jude begins to become <b>very violent</b> and makes some pretty <b>unhealthy choices</b>. She starts fighting back by challenging people to duels and then it’s all downhill from there. It’s at this point that we witness Jude’s descent from your run-of-the-mill YA protagonist to an <i>utterly ruthless</i> <b>antiheroine</b>. Her childhood bully, Prince Cardan, even explicitly recognises how <b>“terrifying”</b> Jude has become. She wants what she wants and she doesn’t care what she has to do or who she has to step on in order to get it…and <i>THAT I RESPECT</i>! <br><br><i>“Father, I am what you made me. I’ve become your daughter after all.”</i><br><br>One of my <b>favourite relationships</b> is, funnily enough, the one between <b>Jude</b> and her foster father, <b>Madoc</b>. She might inherently hate him, as he is the murderer of her parents, but she is also, slowly but surely, turning into <i>his mirror</i>! Of all of his children, she is only one as enthused about duels, swordsmanship, and strategy as he is. In all honesty, I looked forward to all of his interactions with her because you could see how much he <i>genuinely</i> does <b>love his girls</b>, even if two of them aren’t biologically his. When he hears of the bullying that Jude endures, he’s basically <i>ready to kill</i> whomever hurt her. What a great, <i>if slightly bloodthirsty</i>, dad! Gah! I love them <i>SO MUCH</i>! This is a perfectly <b>morally grey</b> familial bond, and I am so grateful to Holly for actually including <i>parental figures</i> in this trilogy. They always tend to conveniently disappear in YA literature, for some reason. *shrugs* I hope that we see just as much, if not more, scenes with the two of them in the next instalment! <br><br><i>“Most of all, I hate you because I think of you. Often. It's disgusting, and I can't stop.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547360255ra/26909351.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Cardan</b>. Oh, Cardan. Just where do I begin? ;) When we first encounter Cardan, he is nothing more than a common <b>bully</b>. But then, as the novel develops and the plot thickens, we begin to see that there is <i>MUCH MORE</i> beneath the surface. Cardan, in comparison with Jude, is only <i>KIND OF</i> <b>terrible</b>. Jude, on the other hand, surpasses him completely. He makes the appearance of being terrifying, whereas Jude actually <i>IS</i>. In addition, he, like Jude, is rather tragic, as well. He has an awful home life, is perpetually drunk on wine, and is completely unable to cope with his feelings for Jude. Needless to say, their <b>sexual tension</b> was so hot that I’m surprised that <i>the pages of my book didn’t catch on fire</i>. They take the <b>enemies-to-lovers</b> trope to new heights, and I thought Magnus and Cleo from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_" title="Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Kingdoms</a> had sexual magnetism! Oof! Never have I been so invested in a YA ship before. But I am <i>ALL ABOARD</i> for <b>#Jardan</b>!!! There better be more kissy-kissy scenes in the next book, or I shall confront Holly with <i>ALL</i> of my grievances!!! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547360255ra/26909352.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As is the case with most of Holly’s novels, we were blessed with quite a few <b>cameos</b> from her previous books! My favourite, of course, being my faery crush, <b>Roiben</b>. What a <i>sexy faery</i>…sigh. If only Kaye would let me have him. That’d be the dream! :D<br><br><i>“I have lied and I have betrayed and I have triumphed. If only there was someone to congratulate me.”</i><br><br>I’m not even going to discuss <b>Locke and Taryn</b>. Those <i>pathetic wastes of space</i> don’t even deserve the energy that I’ll use to type. They deserve each other and I hope that they’ll be <i>completely miserable</i> for the rest of their sorry lives!<br><br>So…I’m going to go and read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032887.The_Wicked_King__The_Folk_of_the_Air___2_" title="The Wicked King (The Folk of the Air, #2) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wicked King</a> now. And then I shall mourn the fact that I have to essentially wait <b>two years</b> for the finale of this <i>AMAZING</i> trilogy! I’m not even going to bother recommending this series. Anyone who hasn’t read it should just feel ashamed of themselves and go remedy that <i>IMMEDIATELY</i>!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547360255ra/26909353.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="102316021022492212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
